that we make. These factors also include, without limitation, those set forth in Exhibit&nbsp;99 to this Form&nbsp;10-K, which are expressly incorporated by reference herein. We do not
intend to update information contained in any forward-looking statements we make. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Results of Operations  </B></FONT></P>

<UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I> Fiscal Year Ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 Compared to Fiscal Year Ended September&nbsp;30, 2000  </I></B></FONT></P>

</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Product Revenue.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Product revenue increased by $8.4&nbsp;million or 37% from $22.4&nbsp;million to
$30.8&nbsp;million. The increase was attributable to $6.1&nbsp;million of increased revenue from Power Systems, of which Ling
Electronics accounted for $4.9&nbsp;million, magnetic levitation products and high-performance motors accounted for $666,000 and power products accounted for $521,000, primarily as a result of our
acquisition of Inverpower. $2.3&nbsp;million of increased revenue was attributable to Semiconductor Products. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Funded research and development and other revenue.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Funded research and development and other revenue increased by
$2.3&nbsp;million or 26% from $8.6&nbsp;million to $10.9&nbsp;million. This increase was primarily attributable to $2.7&nbsp;million in funded research and development revenue from a new
program to develop high power converter assemblies for the U.S. Navy's next generation of modern "all-electric" ships offset by a reduction of $400,000 in funded research and development
revenue from a Department of Energy program to develop low-cost power conversion modules for electric and hybrid-electric vehicles. For the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 and
2000, revenue from commercial contracts, which represents other revenue, is included in funded research and development and other revenue and amounted to $663,000 and $763,000, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost of product revenue.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost of product revenue increased by $8.8&nbsp;million or 46% from $19.1&nbsp;million to
$27.8&nbsp;million. The increase was primarily attributable to the increase in product revenue. In addition, for the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, we provided a $1.2&nbsp;million
reserve for excess and obsolete inventory as compared to $659,000 for the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2000. Gross margin from product revenue as a percentage of product revenue decreased
from 15% to 10%. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Funded research and development and other revenue expenses.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Funded research and development and other revenue expenses
increased by $598,000 or 9</FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>%</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> from $6.8&nbsp;million to $7.4&nbsp;million. The </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>28</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=4,SEQ=28,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=651556,FOLIO='28',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]DE3745A.;17',USER='RHOOKER',CD='21-DEC-2001;11:06' -->
<A NAME="page_de3745_1_29"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
increase was primarily attributable to $1.9&nbsp;million in funded research and development expenses from the U.S. Navy program offset by the reduction of $1.0&nbsp;million of research and
development expenses related to the Department of Energy program. For the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 and 2000, costs and expenses from commercial contracts, which represents other
revenue expenses, are included in funded research and development and other revenue and amounted to $485,000 and $398,000, respectively. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Unfunded research and development expenses.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Unfunded research and development expenses increased by $2.8&nbsp;million
or 80% from $3.5&nbsp;million to $6.2&nbsp;million. The increase is due to increased focus on internally funded research and development projects including the power inverter for an
on-site power generation system and our 250&nbsp;kilowatt and 2.0&nbsp;megawatt UPS and power quality systems. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Selling, general and administrative expenses.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Selling, general and administrative expenses increased by
$3.6&nbsp;million or 36% from $10.0&nbsp;million to $13.6&nbsp;million. The increase was primarily due to an increase in selling expenses associated with the $10.6&nbsp;million increase in
total revenue and the inclusion of Ling Electronics for the entire fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 and Inverpower from July&nbsp;13, 2001 to
September&nbsp;30, 2001. For the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, we provided a $541,000 reserve for doubtful accounts as compared to $266,000 for the fiscal year ended
September&nbsp;30, 2000. In addition, we recorded charges of $223,000, $175,000, $150,000 and $111,000 in settlement of litigation, consolidation of facilities, write-off of impaired
assets and for acceleration of a stock option award vesting schedule, respectively, during the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Write-off of public offering costs.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;On April&nbsp;25, 2001, we converted our registration statement we
initially filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission on October&nbsp;30, 2000 to a shelf registration statement. We have expensed $1.4&nbsp;million of equity financing costs incurred in
connection with the registration statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Amortization of intangibles.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Amortization of intangibles increased by $145,000 or 12% from $1.2&nbsp;million to
$1.4&nbsp;million. The increase was the result of amortization of intangibles recorded in connection with the acquisitions of Ling Electronics in October&nbsp;1999, certain intellectual property
and other intangible assets from Northrop Grumman in November&nbsp;1999 and certain intangible assets from Inverpower Controls&nbsp;Ltd. in July&nbsp;2001. In addition, during 2001, we
wrote-off an impaired intangible asset with a net book value of $61,000. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Net unrealized loss on warrants to purchase common stock.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;During the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, we
began accounting for our warrants to purchase Mechanical Technology Incorporated's common stock and the warrant to purchase Beacon Power's common stock in accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;133, and,
therefore, we have recorded these warrants at their fair value at September&nbsp;30, 2001 and recorded an unrealized loss of $1.5&nbsp;million during the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30,
2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Other income (loss).</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Other income increased to $584,000 or 27% from $460,000. The increase is the result of cash and
cash equivalents being maintained in interest bearing accounts offset by an increase in interest expense associated with the increase in debt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Loss from Beacon Power Corporation.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Loss from Beacon Power Corporation increased by $4.2&nbsp;million from $899,000
to $5.1&nbsp;million. In connection with Beacon Power's initial public offering in November&nbsp;2000, our investment in Beacon Power and additional paid-in-capital was
written up to reflect our beneficial interest in the book value of the stockholders' equity of Beacon Power, which was approximately $16.6&nbsp;million, less losses previously recorded in connection
with the put right obligation in the amount of $5.8&nbsp;million for a net gain of $10.7&nbsp;million. After the write-up of our investment in Beacon Power, we continued to account for
our investment in Beacon Power under the equity method </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>29</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>

<A NAME="page_de3745_1_30"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
of accounting and recorded our share of losses of $5.1&nbsp;million from Beacon Power for the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cumulative effect of change in accounting principle.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;On October&nbsp;1, 2000, we began accounting for our warrants to
purchase Mechanical Technology Incorporated common stock in accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;133 and, therefore, recorded a cumulative unrealized loss of $1.0&nbsp;million as of October&nbsp;1,
2000. On June&nbsp;30, 2001, we began accounting for warrants to purchase our common stock that are designated as a liability in accordance with EITF 00-19, "Accounting for Derivative
Financial Instruments Indexed to, and Potentially Settled in, a Company's Own Stock", and, therefore, recorded a cumulative unrealized gain of $854,000 as of June&nbsp;30, 2001 to record the
warrants at fair value. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Product revenue.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Product revenue increased by $13.3&nbsp;million or 146% from $9.1&nbsp;million to
$22.4&nbsp;million. The increase was attributable to $11.3&nbsp;million of increased revenue from Power Systems, of which Ling Electronics accounted for $7.4&nbsp;million, magnetic levitation
products accounted for $2.3&nbsp;million, high-performance motors accounted for $1.3&nbsp;million and power products accounted for $287,000. $2.0&nbsp;million of increased revenue was
attributable to Semiconductor Products. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Funded research and development and other revenue.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Funded research and development and other revenue increased by
$2.3&nbsp;million or 36% from $6.4&nbsp;million to $8.6&nbsp;million. This increase was attributable to an additional $2.4&nbsp;million in funded research and development revenue from a
Department of Energy program to develop low-cost power conversion modules for electric and hybrid-electric vehicles and was partially offset by our increased focus on internally funded
research projects including the development of power conversion products for the distributed power generation market. For the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2000 and 1999, revenue from
commercial contracts, which represents other revenue, is included in funded research and development and other revenue and amounted to $763,000 and $768,000, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost of product revenue.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost of product revenue increased by $9.6&nbsp;million or 100.5% from $9.5&nbsp;million to
$19.1&nbsp;million. The increase was primarily attributable to the increase in product revenue offset by improved plant utilization at MagMotor and Film Microelectronics. Gross margin from product
revenue as a percentage of product revenue increased to 15% from (4%). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Funded research and development and other revenue expenses.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Funded research and development and other revenue expenses
increased by $1.0&nbsp;million or 17.5% from $5.8&nbsp;million to $6.8&nbsp;million. The increase was primarily attributable to an additional $1.8&nbsp;million in funded research and
development expenses related to the Department of Energy program. For the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2000 and 1999, costs and expenses from commercial contracts, which represents other
revenue expenses, are included in funded research and development and other revenue expenses and amounted to $398,000 and $704,000, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Unfunded research and development expenses.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Unfunded research and development expenses increased by $2.7&nbsp;million
or 375.5% from $726,000 to $3.5&nbsp;million. The increase was primarily attributable to an additional $1.1&nbsp;million in unfunded research and development expenses related to the Department of
Energy program. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Selling, general and administrative expenses.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Selling, general and administrative expenses increased by
$1.2&nbsp;million or 13% from $8.8&nbsp;million to $10.0&nbsp;million. The increase was primarily due to the inclusion of $2.9&nbsp;million of costs from Ling Electronics, $800,000 of costs
for facilities and staffing in an effort to meet expected growth and demand for our products and the inclusion of a full year of expenses related to Inductive Components and Lighthouse Software which
were acquired in January&nbsp;1999 and HyComp which was acquired in April&nbsp;1999. These increases were offset by the </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>30</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>

<A NAME="page_de3745_1_31"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
recording of $2.2&nbsp;million of non-cash stock-based compensation expense related to the issuance of stock options and warrants to consultants and $1.0&nbsp;million of additional
reserves for unbilled contract costs and fees and accounts receivable in 1999. Based on the facts and circumstances during 1999, we established a reserve of $521,000 for unbilled contract costs and
fees related to a contract with the Department of the Air Force which was terminable by the Department of the Air Force if it determined that we were in default under the contract as discussed in
Note&nbsp;H to our financial statements. In addition during 1999, we provided $513,000 in reserve for unbilled contract costs and fees and accounts receivable to properly reflect the reserve
requirements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Amortization of intangibles.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Amortization of intangibles increased $846,000 or 228% from $371,000 to
$1.2&nbsp;million. This increase was the result of amortization of intangibles recorded in connection with the acquisitions of Inductive Components and Lighthouse Software in January&nbsp;1999,
Ling Electronics in October&nbsp;1999 and certain intellectual property and other intangible assets from Northrop Grumman in November&nbsp;1999. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Other income (loss).</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Other income increased to $460,000 from $224,000 of other loss. The increase was the result of an
increase in cash and cash equivalents being maintained in interest-bearing accounts and a decrease of interest expense associated with our line of credit. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Loss from Beacon Power Corporation.</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Loss from Beacon Power decreased by $3.4&nbsp;million or 79% from
$4.3&nbsp;million to $899,000. During the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2000, we recorded our share of Beacon Power's losses of $899,000, under the equity method of accounting. As of
December&nbsp;31, 1999, our investment in Beacon Power had been reduced to zero, however, we continued to record losses from Beacon Power to the extent of additional interest accrued on the
contingent obligation to the class&nbsp;D preferred stockholders of Beacon Power. During the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 1999, we recorded 100% of Beacon Power's losses of
$3.6&nbsp;million in accordance with SAB Topic 5.E., in a manner similar to the equity method of accounting through May&nbsp;1999 and in June&nbsp;1999, we began
accounting for our investment in Beacon Power under the equity method of accounting and recorded our share of Beacon Power's losses of $734,000 from June&nbsp;1999 to September&nbsp;1999. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="page_dk3745_1_33"> </A> </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><B>Liquidity and Capital Resources  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Since inception, we have financed our operations and met our capital expenditure requirements primarily through the sale of private equity securities, public
security offerings, borrowings on our expired line of credit and capital equipment leases. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As
of September&nbsp;30, 2001, our cash, cash equivalents and marketable securities were $20.9&nbsp;million, an increase of $12.1&nbsp;million from September&nbsp;30, 2000.
Cash used in operating activities for the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 was $11.0&nbsp;million as compared to $5.5&nbsp;million in 2000. Cash used in operating activities during the
fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 was primarily attributable to our net loss offset by non-cash items such as depreciation and amortization, increases in allowances for
uncollectible accounts and excess and obsolete inventory, loss from Beacon Power, net unrealized loss from warrants to purchase common stock, write-off of impaired assets, amortization of prepaid
consulting costs, non-cash compensation expense, common stock issued in connection with a settlement agreement, cumulative effect of changes in accounting principles and changes in working capital. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cash
used in investing activities during the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 was $11.8&nbsp;million as compared to $2.9&nbsp;million in 2000. Net cash used in
investing activities during the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 included purchases of marketable securities of $9.8&nbsp;million and capital expenditures of $2.2&nbsp;million. We
estimate that we will spend an additional $2.0&nbsp;million on capital expenditures through fiscal year 2002 primarily at our Power Systems Division to expand our capacity to manufacture our power
conversion products. We expect these additions will be financed principally from lease financing and, to a lesser extent, cash on hand. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cash
provided by financing activities for the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 was $25.1&nbsp;million as compared to $14.7&nbsp;million in 2000. Net cash provided by
financing activities during the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 includes $17.1&nbsp;million of proceeds from the sale of common stock, $7.0&nbsp;million from the exercise of common
stock options and warrants and $1.5&nbsp;million of proceeds from lease financing offset by $446,000 of repayment of long-term debt. In December&nbsp;2000, we completed financing under
an agreement for the lease of certain production equipment in the amount of $1.5&nbsp;million previously entered into in August&nbsp;2000. Payments are due in monthly installments of $40,000 from
October&nbsp;2001 through January&nbsp;2002 and $19,705 from February&nbsp;2002 through November&nbsp;2005. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
anticipate that the existing $20.9&nbsp;million in cash, cash equivalents and marketable securities will be sufficient to fund operations for at least the next twelve months.
However, there can be no assurance that we will not require additional financings within this time frame or that any additional financing, if needed, will be available to us on terms acceptable to us,
if at all. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Factors Affecting Future Results  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our future results remain difficult to predict and may be affected by a number of factors which could cause actual results to differ materially from
forward-looking statements contained in this Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K and presented elsewhere by management from time to time. These factors include business conditions within the
distributed power, power quality, aerospace, transportation, industrial, utility, telecommunications, silicon wafer manufacturing, factory automation, aircraft and automotive industries and the world
economies as a whole, and competitive pressures that may impact research and development spending. Our revenue growth is dependent on technology developments and contract research and development for
both the government and commercial sectors and no assurance can be given that these investments will continue or that we will be able to obtain such funds. In addition, our growth opportunities are
dependent on the introduction of new products that must penetrate distributed power, power quality, aerospace, transportation, industrial, utility, telecommunications, silicon wafer manufacturing,
factory automation, aircraft and automotive markets. No assurance can be given that new products can be developed, or if developed, will be successful; that </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>33</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=33,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=16615,FOLIO='33',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]DK3745A.;14',USER='PKOLLMA',CD='21-DEC-2001;00:35' -->
<A NAME="page_dk3745_1_34"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
competitors will not force prices to an unacceptably low level or take market share from us; or that we can achieve or maintain profits in these or any new markets. Because of these and other factors,
past financial performance should not be considered an indicator of future performance. Investors should not use historical trends to anticipate future results and should be aware that the market
price of our common stock experiences significant volatility. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Effects of Inflation  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We believe that inflation and changing prices over the past three years have not had a significant impact on our net revenue or on our income from continuing
operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Recent Accounting Pronouncements  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In July&nbsp;2001, the Financial Accounting Standards Board issued Statement No.&nbsp;141, "Accounting for Business Combinations", and Statement
No.&nbsp;142, "Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets." These statements modify accounting for business combinations after June&nbsp;30, 2001 and will affect our treatment of goodwill and other
intangible assets at the start of the fiscal year ending September&nbsp;30, 2002; however, business combinations completed after June&nbsp;30, 2001 should apply the new accounting guidelines. The
statements require that goodwill existing at the date of adoption be reviewed for possible impairment and that impairment tests be periodically repeated, with impaired assets written down to fair
value. Additionally, existing goodwill and intangible assets must be assessed and classified
within the Statement's criteria. Intangible assets with estimated useful lives will continue to be amortized over those periods. Amortization of goodwill and intangible assets with indeterminable
lives will cease. At this time, we have not determined the complete impact of SFAS No.&nbsp;142. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
August 2001, the FASB issued SFAS No.&nbsp;144, Accounting for the Impairment or Disposal of Long Lived Assets, which supersedes SFAS No.&nbsp;121, Accounting for the
Impairment of Long-Lived Assets and for Long-Lived Assets to be Disposed of, and the accounting and reporting provisions of APB No.&nbsp;30, SFAS No.&nbsp;144 addresses financial accounting and
reporting for the impairment or disposal of long-lived assets and is effective for fiscal years beginning after December&nbsp;15, 2001, and interim periods within those fiscal years. We are
currently reviewing this statement to determine its effect on our financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Item 7A. QUANTITATIVE AND QUALITATIVE DISCLOSURES ABOUT MARKET RISK.  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We develop products in the United States and sell them worldwide. As a result, our financial results could be affected by factors such as changes in foreign
exchange rates or weak economic conditions in foreign markets. Since our sales are currently priced in U.S. dollars and are translated to local currency amounts, a strengthening of the dollar could
make our products less competitive in foreign markets. Interest income is sensitive to changes in the general level of U.S. interest rates, particularly since our investments are in
short-term instruments. Based on the nature and current levels of our investments, however, we have concluded that there is no material market risk exposure. </FONT></P>

<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>REPORT OF INDEPENDENT PUBLIC ACCOUNTANTS    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>To
the Board of Directors of<BR>
SatCon Technology Corporation: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of SatCon Technology Corporation and its subsidiaries (the Company) (a Delaware corporation) as of September&nbsp;30,
2001 and 2000 and the related consolidated statements of operations, changes in stockholders' equity and comprehensive loss and cash flows for each of the three years in the period ended
September&nbsp;30, 2001. These financial statements are the responsibility of the Company's management. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audits. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
conducted our audits in accordance with auditing standards generally accepted in the United States. Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable
assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement. An audit includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial
statements. An audit also includes assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. We believe
that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
our opinion, the financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of SatCon Technology Corporation and its subsidiaries as of
September&nbsp;30, 2001 and 2000 and the results of their operations and their cash flows for each of the three years in the period ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 in conformity with auditing
standards generally accepted in the United States. </FONT></P>

<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2><B>SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION<BR>  <BR>    NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS    <BR>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>A.&nbsp;&nbsp;
ORGANIZATION AND SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Organization  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;SatCon Technology Corporation (the "Company" or "SatCon") was organized as a Massachusetts corporation in February&nbsp;1985 and reincorporated in Delaware
in 1992. SatCon develops enabling technologies for the emerging digital power marketplace which includes UPS systems, distributed power generation and power quality markets. SatCon also manufactures
power and energy management products that convert, store and manage electricity for businesses and consumers that require high-quality, uninterruptible power. SatCon is utilizing its
engineering and manufacturing expertise to develop products that serve the digital power marketplace, including UPS systems, power generation and power quality products, industrial automation motors
and controls, power electronics and controls, components for fuel cell and microturbine power generation systems, hybrid-electric vehicles and flywheel energy storage systems. SatCon believes the
family of products it is developing will be integral components of distributed power generation and power quality systems. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;SatCon
has expanded its business and capabilities through the following acquisitions: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>K&amp;D
Magmotor Corp.&#151;a manufacturer of custom electric motors, acquired in January&nbsp;1997.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Film
Microelectronics,&nbsp;Inc. ("FMI")&#151;a manufacturer of hybrid microelectronics, acquired in April&nbsp;1997.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Inductive
Components,&nbsp;Inc.&#151;a value-added supplier of customized electric motors, acquired in January&nbsp;1999.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lighthouse
Software,&nbsp;Inc.&#151;a supplier of control software for machine tools, acquired in January&nbsp;1999.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>HyComp,&nbsp;Inc.&#151;a
manufacturer of electronic multi-chip modules, acquired in April&nbsp;1999.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Ling
Electronics,&nbsp;Inc.&#151;a manufacturer of test equipment, power converters, amplifiers and converters, acquired in October&nbsp;1999.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Inverpower
Controls&nbsp;Ltd.&#151;a manufacturer of power electronics modules and advanced high-speed digital controls, acquired in
July&nbsp;2001. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;All
of these acquisitions were accounted for using the purchase method of accounting. In addition, in November&nbsp;1999, the Company acquired intellectual property, tooling and
other assets from Northrop Grumman Corporation. See Note&nbsp;O. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Basis of Consolidation  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The consolidated financial statements include the accounts of SatCon and its majority-owned subsidiaries. All intercompany accounts and transactions have been
eliminated in consolidation. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Foreign Currency Translation  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The functional currency of the Company's foreign subsidiary is the local currency. Assets and liabilities of foreign subsidiaries are translated at the rates
in effect at the balance sheet date, while stockholders' equity (deficit) is translated at historical rates. Statements of operations and cash flow amounts are translated at the average rate for the
period. Translation adjustments are included as a component of accumulated other comprehensive loss. Foreign currency gains and losses arising from transactions are reflected in the loss from
operations and were not significant during the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2001 and 2000. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>42</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=42,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=784584,FOLIO='42',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]FQ3745A.;20',USER='PKOLLMA',CD='21-DEC-2001;00:36' -->
<A NAME="page_fq3745_1_43"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Revenue Recognition  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company recognizes revenue from product sales in accordance with Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) No.&nbsp;101, "Revenue Recognition." Product revenue is
recognized when there is persuasive evidence of an arrangement, the fee is fixed or determinable, delivery of the product to the customer has occurred and the Company has determined that collection of
the fee is probable. Title to the product generally passes upon shipment of the product as the products are shipped FOB shipping point except for certain foreign shipments. If the product requires
installation to be performed by the Company, all revenue related to the product is deferred and recognized upon the completion of the installation. The Company provides for a warranty reserve at the
time the product revenue is recognized. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company performs funded research and development and product development for commercial companies and government agencies under both cost reimbursement and fixed-price contracts.
Product development revenue is included in product revenue. Cost reimbursement contracts provide for the reimbursement of allowable costs and, in some situations, the payment of a fee. These contracts
may contain incentive clauses providing for increases or decreases in the fees depending on how costs compare with a budget. On fixed-price contracts, revenue is generally recognized on the percentage
of completion method based upon the proportion of costs incurred to the total estimated costs for the contract. Revenue from reimbursement contracts is recognized as the services are performed. In
each type of contract, the Company receives periodic progress payments or payments upon reaching interim milestones. All payments to the Company for work performed on contracts with agencies of the
U.S. government are subject to audit and adjustment by the Defense Contract Audit Agency. Adjustments are recognized in the period made. When the current estimates of total contract revenue for
commercial product development contracts indicate a loss, a provision for the entire loss on the contract is recorded. Any losses incurred in performing funded research and development projects are
recognized as research and development expense as incurred. As of September&nbsp;30, 2001 and 2000, the Company has accrued $75,000 and $150,000, respectively, for anticipated contract losses on
commercial contracts. For the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, 2000 and 1999, revenue from commercial contracts, which represents other revenue, is included in funded research and
development and other revenue and amounted to $662,614, $763,023 and $767,954, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost
of product revenue includes cost of product revenue including material, labor and overhead. Costs incurred in connection with funded research and development and other revenue
arrangements are included in research and development and other revenue expenses. For the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, 2000 and 1999, costs and expenses from commercial contracts,
which represents other revenue expenses, are included in funded research and development and other revenue expenses and amounted to $484,982, $397,527 and $704,347, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Deferred
revenue consists of payments received from customers in advance of services performed, product shipped or installation completed. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Cash and Cash Equivalents  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cash and cash equivalents include demand deposits and highly liquid investments with maturities of three months or less when acquired. Cash equivalents are
stated at cost, which approximates market value. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Marketable Securities  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company accounts for marketable securities in accordance with Statement of Financial Accounting Standards (SFAS) No.&nbsp;115. "Accounting for Certain
Investments in Debt and Equity Securities." In accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;115, investments are classified as held to maturity, available for sale or trading. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>43</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=43,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=282536,FOLIO='43',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]FQ3745A.;20',USER='PKOLLMA',CD='21-DEC-2001;00:36' -->
<A NAME="page_fq3745_1_44"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Management determines the appropriate classification of its investments in marketable securities at the time of purchase and re-evaluates such determination at each
balance sheet date. Debt securities for which the Company does not have the intent or ability to hold to maturity are classified as available for sale. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Securities
available for sale are carried at fair value, based on quoted market prices, with the unrealized gains and losses, net of tax, reported in a separate component of
stockholders' equity except for unrealized losses determined to be permanent in nature. Such unrealized losses are included in the determination of net income in the period in which management
determines the decline to be permanent. The Company is not actively involved in the purchase and sale of investments classified as trading. At September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company had no investments
that qualified as trading or held to maturity. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
amortized cost of debt securities classified as available for sale is adjusted for amortization of premiums and accretion of discounts to maturity. Such amortization and interest
are included in interest income. Realized gains and losses are included in other income or loss. The cost of securities sold is based on the specific identification method. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Inventory  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Inventories are stated at the lower of cost or market and costs are determined based on the first-in, first-out method of accounting
and include material, labor and manufacturing overhead costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Property and Equipment  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Property and equipment are stated at cost. Depreciation and amortization is computed using the straight-line method over the asset's estimated
useful life. The estimated useful lives of property and equipment are as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When
assets are retired or otherwise disposed of, the cost and related depreciation and amortization are eliminated from the accounts and any resulting gain or loss is reflected in
other income. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Long-lived Assets  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company periodically evaluates the potential impairment of its long-lived assets whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the
carrying amount of an asset may not be recoverable. At the occurrence of a certain event or change in circumstances or at each balance sheet date, the Company evaluates the potential impairment of an
asset based on future undiscounted cash flows. In the event that impairment exists, the Company will measure the amount of such impairment based on the present value of estimated future cash flows
using a discount rate commensurate with the risks involved.
Factors that management considers in performing this assessment include current operating results, trends and prospects and, in addition, demand, competition and other economic factors. At
September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company determined that the unamortized non-compete agreement component of identifiable intangible assets from the FMI acquisition of $60,737 was no </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>44</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=44,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=760135,FOLIO='44',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]FQ3745A.;20',USER='PKOLLMA',CD='21-DEC-2001;00:36' -->
<A NAME="page_fq3745_1_45"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
longer recoverable and, accordingly, has written this asset off and charged amortization expense. At September&nbsp;30, 2000, the Company determined that there had been no impairment of its
long-lived assets, except as disclosed in Notes&nbsp;E and G. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Intangibles
consisted of the following: </FONT></P>

expense related to intangibles for the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, 2000 and 1999 was $1,374,333, $1,229,815 and $389,685, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Treasury Stock  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company was authorized to repurchase up to 5% of the Company's outstanding shares of common stock through July&nbsp;2000. Under the repurchase program,
the Company purchased 44,500 shares of the Company's outstanding common stock at a cost of $249,704. During the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company retired the 44,500 shares
purchased under the repurchase program. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Use of Estimates  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The preparation of financial statements, in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States, requires management to make
estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported
amounts of revenue and expenses during the period reported. Actual results could differ from these estimates. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Income Taxes  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company accounts for income taxes in accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;109, "Accounting for Income Taxes," which is the asset and liability method for
accounting and reporting for income taxes. Under SFAS No.&nbsp;109, deferred tax assets and deferred tax liabilities are recognized based on temporary differences between the financial reporting and
income tax basis of assets and liabilities using statutory rates. In addition, SFAS No.&nbsp;109 requires a valuation allowance against net deferred tax assets if, based upon the available evidence,
it is more likely than not that some or all of the deferred tax assets will not be realized. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>45</FONT></P>

<A NAME="page_fq3745_1_46"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Stock-based Compensation  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;SFAS No.&nbsp;123, "Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation," requires the measurement of the fair value of stock options or warrants granted to employees to
be included in the statement of operations or, alternatively, disclosed in the notes to consolidated financial statements. The Company accounts for stock-based compensation of employees under the
intrinsic value method of Accounting Principles Board (APB) Opinion No.&nbsp;25, "Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees," and has elected the disclosure-only alternative under SFAS
No.&nbsp;123. The Company records the fair market value of stock options and warrants granted to non-employees in exchange for services in accordance with Emerging Issues Task Force
(EITF) No.&nbsp;96-18, "Accounting for Equity Instruments That Are Issued to Other Than Employees for Acquiring, or in Conjunction with Selling, Goods or Services," in the consolidated
statement of operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Net Loss per Basic and Diluted Common Share  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company reports net loss per basic and diluted common share in accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;128, "Earnings Per Share," which establishes standards for
computing and presenting earnings per share. Basic earnings per share excludes dilution and is computed by dividing income available to common stockholders by the weighted-average number of common
shares outstanding for the period. Diluted earnings per share reflects the potential dilution that could occur if securities or other contracts to issue common stock were exercised or converted into
common stock or resulted in the issuance of common stock that then shared in the earnings of the Company. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Concentration of Credit Risk  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Financial instruments that subject the Company to concentrations of credit risk principally consist of cash equivalents, marketable securities trade accounts
receivable, unbilled contract costs and amounts receivable from exercise of stock options. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company's trade accounts receivable and unbilled contract costs and fees are primarily from sales to U.S. government agencies and commercial customers. The Company does not
require collateral and has not historically experienced significant credit losses related to receivables or unbilled contract costs and fees from individual customers or groups of customers in any
particular industry or geographic area. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Company deposits its cash and invests in short-term investments primarily through a regional commercial bank and an investment company. Credit exposure to any one
entity is limited by Company policy. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Research and Development Costs  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company expenses research and development costs as incurred. Research and development and other revenue expenses include costs incurred in connection with
both funded research and development and other revenue arrangements and unfunded research and development activities. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Comprehensive Income (Loss)  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Comprehensive income (loss) includes net loss, unrealized gains and losses on marketable securities, valuation adjustment for warrants to purchase shares of
Mechanical Technology Incorporated's common stock and foreign currency translation adjustments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Fair Value of Financial Instruments  </I></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company's financial instruments consist of cash and cash equivalents, marketable securities, accounts receivable, unbilled contract costs and fees,
warrants to purchase shares of common stock, </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>46</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=5,SEQ=46,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=351097,FOLIO='46',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]FQ3745A.;20',USER='PKOLLMA',CD='21-DEC-2001;00:36' -->
<A NAME="page_fq3745_1_47"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
accounts payable, debt instruments and contingent obligation to Class&nbsp;D preferred stockholders of Beacon Power Corporation. The estimated fair values of these financial instruments approximate
their carrying values at September&nbsp;30, 2001 and 2000. The estimated fair values have been determined through information obtained from market sources and management estimates. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Accounting for Derivative Instruments  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On October&nbsp;1, 2000, the Company adopted SFAS No.&nbsp;133, "Accounting for Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities," which establishes a new
model for accounting for derivatives and hedging activities. It requires an entity to recognize all derivatives as either assets or liabilities in the statement of financial position and measure these
instruments at fair value. Upon adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;133, the Company recorded an unrealized loss on its investment in derivatives, consisting of warrants to purchase Mechanical Technology
Incorporated common stock in its results of operations as a cumulative effect of a change in accounting principle of $1,021,725 to reflect the impact of adopting this accounting standard on
October&nbsp;1, 2000. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
September&nbsp;2000, the Emerging Issues Task Force issued EITF 00-19, "Accounting for Derivative Financial Instruments Indexed to, and Potentially Settled in, a
Company's Own Stock," which requires freestanding contracts that are settled in a company's own stock, including common stock warrants, to be designated as an equity instrument, asset or a liability.
Under the provisions of EITF 00-19, a contract designated as an asset or a liability must be carried at fair value, with any changes in fair value recorded in the results of operations. A
contract designated as an equity instrument must be included within equity, and no fair value adjustments are required. In accordance with EITF 00-19, the Company has determined that
outstanding warrants as of September&nbsp;30, 2001 to purchase 100,000 shares of the Company's Common Stock issued to Mechanical Technology Incorporated should be designated as a liability and
warrants to purchase 605,050 shares of the Company's Common Stock are designated as an equity instrument. Effective June&nbsp;30, 2001, all warrants designated as a liability must be recorded as a
liability and therefore, the Company reclassified the warrants designated as a liability from equity to liabilities, which had a fair value on the issuance date of $1,505,421, using the Black-Scholes
option-pricing model. At September&nbsp;30, 2001, the outstanding warrants designated as a liability, as a result of the warrant holders having rights that rank higher than those of common
stockholders, have been recorded at a fair value of $234,699 through a reduction of $1,270,722 in the fair value included in the results of operations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Accounting for Beneficial Conversion Feature  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In November&nbsp;2000, the Emerging Issues Task Force issued EITF 00-27, "Application of Issue No.&nbsp;98-5 to Certain Convertible
Instruments," which provides guidance on the calculation of a beneficial conversion feature on a convertible instrument. Based upon the guidance provided in EITF 00-27, the Company has
determined that the redeemable preferred stock issued in August&nbsp;1999 and converted into the Company's Common Stock in March 2000 had a beneficial conversion feature of $1,940,798. Under the
guidance of EITF 00-27, the Company was required to record the beneficial conversion feature of $1,940,798 as a cumulative effect of a change in accounting principle upon adoption during
the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="page_fr3745_1_48"> </A> </FONT> <FONT SIZE=2><I>Reclassifications  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Certain prior-year balances have been reclassified to conform to current-year presentations. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Recent Accounting Pronouncements  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In July&nbsp;2001, the Financial Accounting Standards Board ("FASB") issued SFAS No.&nbsp;141, "Accounting for Business Combinations," and Statement
No.&nbsp;142, "Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets." These statements modify accounting for business combinations after June&nbsp;30, 2001 and will affect the Company's treatment of goodwill and
other intangible assets at the start of the fiscal year 2002; however, business combinations completed after June&nbsp;30, 2001 should apply the new accounting guidelines. The statements require
that goodwill existing at the date of adoption be reviewed for possible impairment and that impairment tests be periodically repeated, with impaired assets written down to fair value. Additionally,
existing goodwill and intangible assets must be assessed and classified within the Statement's criteria. Intangible assets with estimated useful lives will continue to be amortized over those periods.
Amortization of goodwill and intangible assets with indeterminable lives will cease. At this time, the Company has not determined the complete impact of SFAS No.&nbsp;142. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As
of September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company has goodwill with a net book value of $6,234,653. The Company has decided to early adopt SFAS No.&nbsp;142 as of October&nbsp;1, 2001
and therefore, this goodwill will no longer be amortized. During the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, 2000 and 1999, the Company recorded $638,864, $609,855 and $93,576, respectively, of
amortization expense related to this goodwill. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
August 2001, the FASB issued SFAS No.&nbsp;144, "Accounting for the Impairment or Disposal of Long Lived Assets," which supersedes SFAS No.&nbsp;121, "Accounting for the
Impairment of Long-Lived Assets and for Long-Lived Assets to be Disposed Of," and the accounting and reporting provisions of APB No.&nbsp;30. SFAS No.&nbsp;144 addresses financial accounting and
reporting for the impairment or disposal of long-lived assets and is effective for fiscal years beginning after December&nbsp;15, 2001, and interim periods within those fiscal years. The Company is
currently reviewing this statement to determine its effect on the Company's financial statements. </FONT></P>

of September&nbsp;30, 2001, marketable securities consisted of the following: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As
of September&nbsp;30, 2001 and 2000, there was $1,810,503 and $19,903 of property under capital leases included in machinery and equipment, respectively. Of these capital leases,
$1,459,750 relates to asset purchases made during the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2000 for which the Company entered into a sale leaseback transaction during the fiscal year ended
September&nbsp;30, 2001. As of September&nbsp;30, 2001 and 2000, there was $29,910 of property under capital leases that were included in computer software. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company consolidated its FMI manufacturing facilities, and as a result, has written-off the net book value of
the leasehold improvements of the vacated premise of $32,767, which has been included in cost of product revenue. During the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 1999, the Company determined that
certain of its machinery and equipment with a net book value totaling $105,544 was impaired based on a significant change in the manner in which the asset was used, and such assets were
written-off during the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 1999. These assets included $86,492 of tooling costs associated with the introduction of brushless motor products at the
Company's MagMotor Division that were impaired based on design changes in the product and $19,052 of optics equipment at the Company's Technology Center that were abandoned. These impairment losses
have been included in cost of product revenue and unfunded research and development expenses, respectively. </FONT></P>

<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=49,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=323235,FOLIO='49',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]FR3745A.;35',USER='LPALLES',CD='21-DEC-2001;13:30' -->
<A NAME="page_fr3745_1_50"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>F.&nbsp;&nbsp;INVESTMENT IN BEACON POWER CORPORATION  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 1999 and 2000 and substantially all of the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company
accounted for its investment in Beacon Power under the equity method of accounting. During the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, 2000 and 1999, the Company recorded $5,065,034, $899,493
and $4,340,567, respectively, of losses from Beacon Power, representing the Company's share of losses up to the extent of committed capital. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
November&nbsp;17, 2000, Beacon Power listed its common stock on the Nasdaq National Market. In connection with the listing, the put right granted to the Class&nbsp;D preferred
stockholders of Beacon Power was terminated and the contingent obligation to Class&nbsp;D preferred stockholders of Beacon Power was reclassified to additional paid-in capital. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
November&nbsp;22, 2000, Beacon Power completed an initial public offering of its common stock and issued 8,000,000 shares of its common stock at $6.00 per share. Upon the closing
of Beacon Power's initial public offering, each share of Beacon Power's class&nbsp;A, C, D, E and F preferred stock was converted into two shares of Beacon Power's common stock, or 29,359,530 shares
of common stock, of which the Company received 9,691,440 shares of Beacon Power's common stock. In addition, upon the closing of Beacon Power's initial public offering, Beacon Power issued 873,794
shares of common stock in payment for consulting fees and accrued dividends on Beacon Power's class&nbsp;D and E preferred stock, of which the Company received 11,098 shares of Beacon Power's common
stock. After these events, the Company owned approximately 25.0% of Beacon Power's outstanding voting stock. In accordance with SAB No.&nbsp;51, the Company's investment in Beacon Power and
additional paid-in capital was written up to reflect its beneficial interest in the book value of the stockholders' equity of Beacon Power at November&nbsp;22, 2000, which was
$14,988,382, less losses previously recorded in connection with the put right obligation in the amount of $5,831,879 for a net gain of $9,156,503. On December&nbsp;19, 2000, Beacon Power issued an
additional 1,200,000 shares of its common stock at $6.00 per share to cover over-allotments. Upon the issuance of the additional 1,200,000 shares, the Company owned approximately 24.2% of
Beacon Power's outstanding voting stock. The Company's investment in Beacon Power and additional paid-in capital was written up in accordance with SAB No.&nbsp;51 to reflect its
beneficial interest in the increase in book value of the stockholders' equity of Beacon Power at December&nbsp;19, 2000, which was $1,622,721. On December&nbsp;20, 2000, Beacon Power issued
985,507 shares of its common stock in connection with the cashless exercise of warrants to purchase shares of Beacon Power's common stock. Upon the issuance of the additional 985,507 shares, the
Company owned approximately 23.7% of Beacon Power's outstanding voting stock. On December&nbsp;22, 2000, Beacon Power issued 997,369 shares of its common stock in connection with the cashless
exercise of warrants to purchase shares of Beacon Power's common stock. Upon the issuance of the additional 997,369 shares, the Company owned approximately 23.1% of Beacon Power's outstanding voting
stock. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;After
the write-up of its investment in Beacon Power, the Company continued to account for its investment in Beacon Power under the equity method of accounting and
recorded its share of losses from Beacon Power on a one fiscal quarter trailing basis. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
September&nbsp;28, 2001, the Company distributed 5,000,000 shares of Beacon Power common stock to its stockholders. Upon the distribution of the 5,000,000 shares, the Company
recorded the distribution of the 5,000,000 shares as a reduction of additional paid-in-capital based on the book value per share prior to the distribution, or $0.59 per share.
After the distribution, the Company owned approximately 11.0% of Beacon Power's outstanding voting stock. Additionally, the Company has determined that it does not have the ability to exercise
significant influence over the operating and financial policies of Beacon Power and, therefore, now accounts for its investment in Beacon Power using the fair value method as set forth in SFAS
No.&nbsp;115, "Accounting for Certain Debt and Equity Securities." The Company is no longer required to record its share of any losses from Beacon Power and the investment is carried at fair value
and designated as available for sale and any unrealized </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>50</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=50,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=709923,FOLIO='50',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]FR3745A.;35',USER='LPALLES',CD='21-DEC-2001;13:30' -->
<A NAME="page_fr3745_1_51"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
holding gains or losses to be included in stockholders' equity as a component of accumulated other comprehensive income/(loss). As of September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Beacon Power common stock had a
fair value of $7,152,983 and the Company recorded an unrealized gain of $4,364,035 in stockholders' equity as a component of accumulated other comprehensive income/(loss). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Additionally,
the Company has a warrant to purchase 173,704 shares of Beacon Power's common stock that has an exercise price of $1.25 per share and expires in 2005. The Company
accounts for this warrant in accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;133 and, therefore, records the warrant at its fair value. As of September&nbsp;30, 2001, the warrant to purchase Beacon Power common
stock had a fair value of $201,436 and is included in warrants to purchase common stock on the accompanying balance sheet. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Beacon
Power accounted for $242,460, $470,996 and $72,644 of the Company's total revenue for the fiscal years ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively. At
September&nbsp;30, 2001 and 2000, the Company had $172,598 and $346,066, respectively, of accounts receivable and unbilled contract costs and fees from Beacon Power. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
March&nbsp;1, 1999, the Company reached a definitive settlement arrangement with Albert R. Snider (the "Settlement Agreement"), the holder of a note payable that commenced on
April&nbsp;16, 1997, regarding a suit filed against Mr.&nbsp;Snider for breach of certain representations made by him, including statements of inventory balances in the Asset Purchase Agreement
dated as of April&nbsp;3, 1997 between FMI and Mr.&nbsp;Snider relating to the purchase of the business of FMI and a counterclaim filed by Mr.&nbsp;Snider seeking, among other things, payments
allegedly due from the Company under a promissory note. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Pursuant
to the terms of the Settlement Agreement, the Company made a $100,000 cash payment to Mr.&nbsp;Snider on March&nbsp;9, 1999 and the parties executed mutual general
releases dismissing any and all claims between them. In addition, the Settlement Agreement provides a right of first refusal in favor of the Company with respect to certain shares of the Company's
Common Stock, beneficially owned by Mr.&nbsp;Snider. Concurrently with the execution of the Settlement Agreement, the Company and Mr.&nbsp;Snider entered into a consulting agreement pursuant to
which Mr.&nbsp;Snider will perform certain consulting, advisory and related services as the Company may reasonably request from time to time between October&nbsp;1, 1999 and October&nbsp;1,
2002. In exchange for these services, the Company issued 42,860 shares of its Common Stock to Mr.&nbsp;Snider, which were held by an escrow agent. The Company </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>51</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=4,SEQ=51,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=995000,FOLIO='51',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]FR3745A.;35',USER='LPALLES',CD='21-DEC-2001;13:30' -->
<A NAME="page_fr3745_1_52"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
has recorded these shares held in escrow at market value and as a reduction to stockholders' equity as of September&nbsp;30, 1999. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
April&nbsp;26, 2000, the escrow agent, as authorized by the Company released the 42,860 shares of the Company's Common Stock that were held in escrow to Mr.&nbsp;Snider. The
Company recorded these securities at fair value until they were released from escrow at a market price of $16.00 per share or $685,760. The Company determined that the value of these securities
exceeded the net realizable value of the underlying services to be received by $235,760. The Company has charged this excess amount to selling, general and administrative expenses during the fiscal
year ended September&nbsp;30, 2000. The Company is amortizing the realizable asset of $450,000 over the three-year period of service through September&nbsp;30, 2002. At
September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company determined that the services provided under the consulting agreement will no longer be requested and has written off the unamortized asset of $150,000 to
selling, general and administrative expenses during the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Litigation  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
November&nbsp;6, 1999, APACE, Inc. ("APACE") an action was commenced against the Company in the Supreme Court of the State of New York claiming that the Company had been awarded
a prime contract by the U.S. Department of Energy and that the Company had failed or refused to negotiate a subcontract with APACE, allegedly in breach of a contract between the Company and APACE.
APACE sought in excess of $1,000,000 in damages. The Company denied the allegations, moved to stay the action and filed for arbitration with the American Arbitration Association (the "AAA") in Boston,
Massachusetts. The AAA decided that the arbitration would go forward in Boston. In the meantime APACE requested that the court permit the action to go forward and for the arbitration to be stayed. On
March&nbsp;21, 2000, the Supreme Court of the State of New York issued an order compelling arbitration and staying APACE's action pending arbitration to be conducted by the AAA in Boston. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>52</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=5,SEQ=52,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=351459,FOLIO='52',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]FR3745A.;35',USER='LPALLES',CD='21-DEC-2001;13:30' -->
<A NAME="page_fr3745_1_53"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On June&nbsp;26, 2000, APACE served the Company with an amended answering statement and counterclaim, including additional allegations that the Company had engaged in unfair and
deceptive trade practices and that its actions were willful and knowing. Based on these allegations, APACE sought multiple damages, as well as attorneys' fees and expenses. On July&nbsp;19, 2000,
the Company filed an answer to APACE's amended answering statement and counterclaim, denying the allegations and asserting various affirmative defenses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;An
arbitrator was selected and the arbitration was scheduled to go forward in Boston for nine days in February, March and April of 2001. The parties had exchanged some discovery and
expected to make a further exchange early in 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
February&nbsp;7, 2001, the Company, APACE, Roger M. Slotkin and Jeffrey Waxweiler entered into a settlement agreement with respect to all claims concerning, in connection with or
arising from the APACE litigation and arbitration. The settlement agreement also contained mutual releases of the parties relating to all claims. Pursuant to the settlement agreement, the Company paid
and delivered to APACE $60,000 and issued 12,500 shares of the Company's Common Stock, valued at $13.00 per share or $162,500, to APACE. The Company was not obligated to register these shares under
the Securities Act of 1933, as amended. The AAA was notified that the arbitration proceeding would be dismissed without any recovery by any party, and APACE's counsel filed a voluntary Stipulation of
Dismissal With Prejudice in the Supreme Court for the State of New York on March&nbsp;9, 2001. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;From
time to time, the Company is a party to routine litigation and proceedings in the ordinary course of business. The Company is not aware of any current or pending litigation to
which the Company is or may be a party that the Company believes could materially adversely affect the Company's results of operations or financial condition. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>I. EMPLOYEE BENEFIT PLAN  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company offers a 401(k) Employee Benefit Plan (the "Plan"). Under the Plan, any regular employee, as defined by the Plan, who has completed six months of
service and has attained the age of 21&nbsp;years is eligible to participate. Under the terms of the Plan, an employee may defer up to 15% of his or her compensation through contributions to the
Plan. During 1999, the Company extended the Plan to its wholly-owned subsidiaries. The Company made matching contributions to the Plan of $398,281, $366,264 and $218,729 during the fiscal years ended
September&nbsp;30, 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At
September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company had net operating loss carry-forwards of approximately $46,000,000 and $38,000,000 for federal and state income tax purposes, respectively.
The federal net operating losses expire beginning September&nbsp;30, 2008 through 2021. The state net operating losses will expire beginning September&nbsp;30, 2001 through 2006. The use of these
losses may be limited due to ownership change limitations under Section&nbsp;382 of the Internal Revenue Code. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>K.&nbsp;&nbsp;STOCKHOLDERS' EQUITY  </B></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Investment from Mechanical Technology Incorporated  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On October&nbsp;21, 1999, the Company received a $7,070,000 investment from Mechanical Technology Incorporated ("MTI"). In consideration for MTI's
investment, MTI received 1,030,000 shares of the Company's Common Stock at a discounted price of approximately $6.80 per share, and warrants to purchase an additional 100,000 shares of the Company's
Common Stock at an exercise price of $8.80 per share and an expiration date four years from the date of issuance. MTI funded $2,570,000 of its investment in the Company on October&nbsp;21, 1999 and
received 370,800 of the 1,030,000 shares of the Company's Common Stock and a warrant to purchase 36,000 of the 100,000 shares of the Company's Common Stock. MTI made the remaining investment on
January&nbsp;31, 2000 of $4,500,000 and received the remaining 659,200 shares of the Company's Common Stock and a warrant to purchase the remaining 64,000 shares of the Company's Common Stock. The
Company incurred approximately $95,000 of legal, accounting, consultation and filing fees in connection with this transaction. The Company has valued the warrants issued to MTI on October&nbsp;21,
1999 and January&nbsp;31, 2000, at $231,912 and $1,273,509, respectively, using the Black-Scholes option-pricing model. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In
addition, the Company received a warrant to purchase 108,000 shares of MTI's common stock on October&nbsp;21, 1999 and a warrant to purchase 192,000 shares of MTI's common stock
on January&nbsp;31, 2000 at exercise prices of $12.56 per share, as adjusted to reflect a 3:1 stock split in April&nbsp;2000, and expiration dates four years from the date of issuance. The Company
has valued the warrant received on October&nbsp;21, 1999 and January&nbsp;31, 2000 at $568,553 and $2,926,885, respectively, using the Black-Scholes option-pricing model, and has recorded the
warrants as an asset and additional paid in capital. In accordance with EITF No.&nbsp;96-11, "Accounting for Forward Contracts and Purchased Options to Acquire Securities Covered by FASB
Statement No.&nbsp;115," options that are entered into to purchase securities that will be accounted for under SFAS No.&nbsp;115 should, at inception, be designated as
held-to-maturity, available-for-sale, or trading and accounted for in a manner consistent with the accounting prescribed by SFAS No.&nbsp;115 for that
category of securities. The Company has designated that the securities to be purchased under the warrant agreement will be available-for-sale securities and, therefore, the
Company has marked to market the fair value of the warrants at each reporting period date and has recorded any unrealized gains and losses as a component of accumulated other comprehensive loss
included in stockholders' equity. At September&nbsp;30, 2000, the warrants have an </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>55</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=55,EFW="2065407",CP="SATCON TECHNOLOGY CORPORATION",DN="1",CHK=841970,FOLIO='55',FILE='DISK011:[01BOS5.01BOS3745]FT3745A.;19',USER='RHOOKER',CD='21-DEC-2001;11:06' -->
<A NAME="page_ft3745_1_56"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>
unrealized loss of $1,021,725, which is included in accumulated other comprehensive loss included in stockholders' equity. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
October&nbsp;1, 2000, the Company adopted SFAS No.&nbsp;133, "Accounting for Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities," which establishes a new model for accounting for
derivatives and hedging activities. It requires an entity to recognize all derivatives as either assets or liabilities in the statement of financial position and measure these instruments at fair
value. Upon adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;133, the Company recorded the $1,024,725 unrealized loss on its investment in warrants to purchase MTI's common stock in its results of operations as a
cumulative effect of a change in accounting principle to reflect the impact of adopting this accounting standard on October&nbsp;1, 2000. As of September&nbsp;30, 2001, the warrants to purchase
MTI's common stock have a fair value of $375,479, using the Black-Scholes option-pricing model. During the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company recorded a unrealized loss in its
statement of operations on the warrants to purchase MTI's common stock of $2,098,234. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Stock Options  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Under the Company's 1992, 1994, 1996, 1998, 1999 and 2000 Stock Option Plans (collectively, the "Plans"), both qualified and non-qualified stock
options may be granted to certain officers, employees, directors and consultants to purchase up to 4,250,000 shares of the Company's Common Stock. At September&nbsp;30, 2001, 3,716,752 of the
4,250,000 stock options available for grant under the Plans have been granted. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Plans are subject to the following provisions: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
aggregate fair market value (determined as of the date the option is granted) of the Company's Common Stock that any employee may purchase in any calendar year pursuant to the
exercise of qualified options may not exceed $100,000. No person who owns, directly or indirectly, at the time of the granting of a qualified option to him or her, more than 10% of the total combined
voting power of all classes of stock of the Company shall be eligible to receive any qualified options under the Plans unless the option price is at least 110% of the fair market value of the
Company's Common Stock subject to the option, determined on the date of grant. Non-qualified options are not subject to this limitation. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Qualified
options are issued only to employees of the Company, while non-qualified options may be issued to non-employee directors, consultants and others, as
well as to employees of the Company. Options granted under the Plans may not be granted with an exercise price less than 100% of fair value of the Company's Common Stock, as determined by the Board of
Directors on the grant date. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Options
under the Plans must be granted within 10&nbsp;years from the effective date of the Plan. Qualified options granted under the Plans cannot be exercised more than
10&nbsp;years from the date of grant, except that qualified options issued to 10% or greater stockholders are limited to five-year terms. All options granted under the Plans provide for
the payment of the Company's exercise price in cash, or by delivery to the Company of shares of the Company's Common Stock already owned by the optionee having fair market value equal to the exercise
price of the options being exercised, or by a combination
of such methods of payment. Generally, the options vest and become exercisable ratably over a four-year period. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The
Plans contain antidilutive provisions authorizing appropriate adjustments in certain circumstances. Shares of the Company's Common Stock subject to options that expire without
being exercised or that are canceled as a result of the cessation of employment are available for further grants. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At
September&nbsp;30, 2001, an additional 533,248 shares were available under the Plans for future grants. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
1999, the Company granted fully vested and immediately exercisable options to purchase 755,000 shares of the Company's Common Stock to consultants at exercise prices ranging
from $5.75 to $10.00 per share, of which 300,000 stock options were granted outside of the Plans. The Company has recorded the fair value of the options, as determined by the Black-Scholes option
pricing model, of $2,152,277, to selling, general and administrative expenses during the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;30, 1999. As of September&nbsp;30, 1999, options to purchase 450,000
shares at an exercise price of $7.00 per share were exercised. As of September&nbsp;30, 1999, the Company received $1,333,333 of cash on these exercises and the remaining amount due from the
stockholders is classified within stockholders' equity as amounts receivable from exercise of stock options. As of September&nbsp;30, 2001, options to purchase 750,000 shares at exercise prices
ranging from $5.75 to $10.00 per share have been exercised. As of September&nbsp;30, 2001, the Company has received full payment on these exercises. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During
2000, the Company granted 216,000 non-qualified stock options to employees at an exercise price of $17.56 per share outside of the Board approved Plans, which are
included in the above table. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On
